**Candidate 21:** `c0*exp(A*c1+c2*t) + c3*cos(c4*log(A*c5+c6*t+1))`
exp(A*c1+c2*t) — if c1=0, becomes exp(c2*t), not A*exp(t). cos(log(A+t+1)) — if c6=0, cos(log(A+1)). But cos ≠ sin unless phase shifted... wait, cos(x) = sin(x + π/2). But the argument here is c4*log(A*c5+1), and we need sin(log(A+1)). With c4=1, c5 chosen appropriately, cos(log(A*c5+1)) — but we can't add a phase shift inside cos to make it sin(log(A+1)) because the phase would need to be inside the argument as an additive constant. Actually cos(c4*log(A*c5+c6*t+1)) with c6=0 gives cos(c4*log(A*c5+1)). We need sin(log(A+1)). cos(x) = sin(x+π/2), so cos(log(A+1)) = sin(log(A+1)+π/2) ≠ sin(log(A+1)). Can't match. Also missing sqrt(A) and A*exp(t). No match.

This has cos(c7*log(A*c8+c9*t+1)). If c9=0: cos(c7*log(A*c8+1)). With c7=1, c8 chosen: cos(log(A+1)). But cos(log(A+1)) ≠ sin(log(A+1)). These are different functions. 

Wait — can we use the free constant c7 to create a phase? cos(c7*log(A*c8+1)) — no, c7 multiplies the argument, it doesn't add a phase. So this is cos of a scaled log, not a phase-shifted cos. Can't match sin(log(A+1)).
